        }

          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

        <h2>Email display settings</h2>

        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>

        <p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>

        <p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

<br>



<br>





(1) Tested on linux-chromeOS Asan.



<span class="line"><!---->(1) Tested on linux-chromeOS Asan.<!----></span>



<br>





(2) Force chromeOS to tablet mode pass in command line --force-tablet-mode=touch_view --touch-devices=12 (touch-devices=[int] depends on your computer "$ xinput"). This command is to simulate real device( tablet mode) so there's will be no cursor.



<span class="line"><!---->(2) Force chromeOS to tablet mode pass in command line --force-tablet-mode=touch_view --touch-devices=12 (touch-devices=[int] depends on your computer "$ xinput"). This command is to simulate real device( tablet mode) so there's will be no cursor.<!----></span>



<br>





(3) Add new desk at least one or two desk.



<span class="line"><!---->(3) Add new desk at least one or two desk.<!----></span>



<br>





(4) Open browser and and new tab.



<span class="line"><!---->(4) Open browser and and new tab.<!----></span>



<br>





(5) Swipe up from button to open split view(correct me if I'm wrong).



<span class="line"><!---->(5) Swipe up from button to open split view(correct me if I'm wrong).<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->(5) Drag the new tab to the right side and then remove one desk.<!----></span>

Unrelated to the UAF, but the ownership of `capture_window_` in ash::DragDropTracker seems having problems. ash::DragDropTracker owns it via unique_ptr. But all aura::Window are owned by their parent by default, unless we call set_owned_by_parent(false) to tell it is not the case. It seems CreateCaptureWindow [1] is not doing that. Are we double owning `capture_window_` ?



<span class="line"><!---->Unrelated to the UAF, but the ownership of `capture_window_` in ash::DragDropTracker seems having problems. ash::DragDropTracker owns it via unique_ptr. But all aura::Window are owned by their parent by default, unless we call set_owned_by_parent(false) to tell it is not the case. It seems CreateCaptureWindow [1] is not doing that. Are we double owning `capture_window_` ?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[1] 



<span class="line"><!---->[1] <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:ash/drag_drop/drag_drop_tracker.cc;l=89;drc=2c63db7ef6a10e2958e4847908ec9b2fd03e8ab2;bpv=0;bpt=0



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:ash/drag_drop/drag_drop_tracker.cc;l=89;drc=2c63db7ef6a10e2958e4847908ec9b2fd03e8ab2;bpv=0;bpt=0"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:ash/drag_drop/drag_drop_tracker.cc;l=89;drc=2c63db7ef6a10e2958e4847908ec9b2fd03e8ab2;bpv=0;bpt=0<!----></a>

I'm able to repro a UAF, but the stack traces and objects involved look a bit different:



<span class="line"><!---->I'm able to repro a UAF, but the stack traces and objects involved look a bit different:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When dropping on a desk mini view, we end up in DragDropController::OnMouseEvent. In this function, `translated_target` will be a VirtualDesksWidget which belongs to a hierarchy ultimately owned by the OverviewSession.



<span class="line"><!---->When dropping on a desk mini view, we end up in DragDropController::OnMouseEvent. In this function, `translated_target` will be a VirtualDesksWidget which belongs to a hierarchy ultimately owned by the OverviewSession.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When OnMouseEvent calls DragDropController::Drop, it will trigger a sequence of events that results in the new tab window getting snapped, which exits overview mode. This in turn destroys the hierarchy that VirtualDesksWidget belongs to.



<span class="line"><!---->When OnMouseEvent calls DragDropController::Drop, it will trigger a sequence of events that results in the new tab window getting snapped, which exits overview mode. This in turn destroys the hierarchy that VirtualDesksWidget belongs to.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:ash/drag_drop/drag_drop_controller.cc;l=347;drc=51970fdd244abed4d6388f864b0e97b5260d390f



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:ash/drag_drop/drag_drop_controller.cc;l=347;drc=51970fdd244abed4d6388f864b0e97b5260d390f"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:ash/drag_drop/drag_drop_controller.cc;l=347;drc=51970fdd244abed4d6388f864b0e97b5260d390f<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





We then get to line 356 that calls GetTopLevelWindow on `translated_target` which now points to a destroyed object.



<span class="line"><!---->We then get to line 356 that calls GetTopLevelWindow on `translated_target` which now points to a destroyed object.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:ash/drag_drop/drag_drop_controller.cc;l=356;drc=51970fdd244abed4d6388f864b0e97b5260d390f



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:ash/drag_drop/drag_drop_controller.cc;l=356;drc=51970fdd244abed4d6388f864b0e97b5260d390f"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:ash/drag_drop/drag_drop_controller.cc;l=356;drc=51970fdd244abed4d6388f864b0e97b5260d390f<!----></a>



<br>



<br>



<br>





I don't know what the fix here is going to look like. One interesting tidbit is that there's code in `OverviewController::ToggleOverview` that (I'm guessing) was added to deal with a similar situation:



<span class="line"><!---->I don't know what the fix here is going to look like. One interesting tidbit is that there's code in `OverviewController::ToggleOverview` that (I'm guessing) was added to deal with a similar situation:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





    // Don't delete |overview_session_| yet since the stack is still using it.



<span class="line"><!---->    // Don't delete |overview_session_| yet since the stack is still using it.<!----></span>



<br>





    base::ThreadTaskRunnerHandle::Get()->DeleteSoon(



<span class="line"><!---->    base::ThreadTaskRunnerHandle::Get()-&gt;DeleteSoon(<!----></span>



<br>





        FROM_HERE, overview_session_.release());



<span class="line"><!---->        FROM_HERE, overview_session_.release());<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





however, the widget in question has already been destroyed by `OverviewSession::Shutdown` which is called ~10 lines above.



<span class="line"><!---->however, the widget in question has already been destroyed by `OverviewSession::Shutdown` which is called ~10 lines above.<!----></span>

Re#17: it doesn't seem the crash described in the report and 



<span class="line"><!---->Re#17: it doesn't seem the crash described in the report and <!----></span>





comment#2



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c2"><!---->comment#2<!----></a>





 is the same as what you described in #17 (though we should fix that one if it crashes as well). For the original crash, looks like it happens when dragging a webUI tab to the right side of the screen, and then use keyboard shortcut to remove a desk, in this case it can cause window visibility change, thus calls CleanupGestureState, which then calls CancelActiveTouches to cause the drag being cancelled, thus causes |capture_window_| which is owned by DragDropTracker being destroyed. But CleanupGestureState is still using this window, thus cause the heap-use-after-free crash.



<span class="line"><!----> is the same as what you described in #17 (though we should fix that one if it crashes as well). For the original crash, looks like it happens when dragging a webUI tab to the right side of the screen, and then use keyboard shortcut to remove a desk, in this case it can cause window visibility change, thus calls CleanupGestureState, which then calls CancelActiveTouches to cause the drag being cancelled, thus causes |capture_window_| which is owned by DragDropTracker being destroyed. But CleanupGestureState is still using this window, thus cause the heap-use-after-free crash.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





For the fix, I wonder if we can get a weakptr of the window and if it's no longer valid after CancelActiveTouches, then return directly.



<span class="line"><!---->For the fix, I wonder if we can get a weakptr of the window and if it's no longer valid after CancelActiveTouches, then return directly.<!----></span>

Re#24: It's possible to have physical keyboard in tablet mode. Tablet mode UI mode is decided by the presence of the input device, not the keyboard. Also the crash in #17 does not involve a keyboard though. It's about dragging a tab and dropping it on top of the desk mini view when splitview is active.



<span class="line"><!---->Re#24: It's possible to have physical keyboard in tablet mode. Tablet mode UI mode is decided by the presence of the input device, not the keyboard. Also the crash in #17 does not involve a keyboard though. It's about dragging a tab and dropping it on top of the desk mini view when splitview is active.<!----></span>

Cancelling active touches may, under certain circumstances, end up



<span class="line"><!---->Cancelling active touches may, under certain circumstances, end up<!----></span>



<br>





destroying the window that it was called from. This change adds code



<span class="line"><!---->destroying the window that it was called from. This change adds code<!----></span>



<br>





to detect this and does an early exit if it happens.

Cancelling active touches may, under certain circumstances, end up



<span class="line"><!---->Cancelling active touches may, under certain circumstances, end up<!----></span>



<br>





destroying the window that it was called from. This change adds code



<span class="line"><!---->destroying the window that it was called from. This change adds code<!----></span>



<br>





to detect this and does an early exit if it happens.



<span class="line"><!---->to detect this and does an early exit if it happens.<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.
